## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science & solid mechanics (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which strongly indicates a constitutive law for a solid under mechanical loading with temperature-dependent elasticity/plasticity and thermal strain/softening. Common relationships model sigma as elastic response to mechanical strain offset by thermal expansion and modified by temperature-dependent modulus, yield stress, and hardening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelasticity (thermal strain offset): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (small-strain elastic solid with coefficient of thermal expansion and reference temperature)
- Hooke’s law with temperature-dependent modulus (linear softening): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic modulus varies approximately linearly with temperature over a limited range)
- Hooke’s law with inverse-temperature modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 / (T + c2)) * epsilon (modulus decreases with T and asymptotes at high T)
- Elastic + nonlinear elastic correction (Landau-type): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (moderate-strain nonlinear elasticity; coefficients may be fit at a fixed T)
- Temperature-scaled nonlinear elasticity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elastic response whose stiffness changes with T)
- Power-law hardening with temperature-dependent strength: sigma = (c0 * exp(c1 * T)) * epsilon**c2 (empirical strain hardening where strength parameter changes exponentially with T)
- Power-law hardening with temperature-dependent exponent: sigma = c0 * epsilon**(c1 + c2 * T) (hardening curvature changes with temperature)
- Ramberg–Osgood-type inverted form (stress as function of strain): sigma = c0 * (epsilon)**c1 (simplified monotone nonlinear stress–strain curve when only epsilon is available)
- Thermal softening multiplier (bounded): sigma = (c0 * epsilon**c1) * (c2 / (c2 + exp(c3 * T))) (stress decreases with T with a smooth transition rather than linear drop)
- Yield-like transition via smooth activation in strain: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 * log(1 + exp(c3 * (epsilon - c4))) (elastic then rapid rise/flow after a characteristic strain; temperature shifts stiffness/offset)
- Exponential-in-strain stiffening with thermal modulation: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (exp(c2 * epsilon) - 1) (polymer/elastomer-like stiffening; temperature scales effective modulus)
- Thermoelastic with quadratic thermal strain correction: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2) - c3 * (T - c2)**2) (thermal expansion nonlinearity across a wider temperature range)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-strain elastic regime → sigma proportional to epsilon with slope interpreted as an effective modulus; temperature dependence often enters as E(T)*epsilon.
- Thermal expansion compensation → sigma depends on (epsilon - alpha*(T-T0)); if stress vanishes at free expansion, the model should allow sigma≈0 when epsilon≈alpha*(T-T0).
- Thermal softening of stiffness/strength → multiplicative factors that decrease with T (e.g., E(T) or strength(T)) are common; linear-in-T works locally, smooth bounded forms avoid negative stiffness.
- Nonlinear elasticity/hardening at larger strain → add higher powers of epsilon (epsilon**2, epsilon**3) or exponential-in-epsilon to capture curvature of the stress–strain curve.
- Changing hardening curvature with temperature → allow the exponent on epsilon to vary with T (epsilon**(n(T))) to represent temperature-driven changes in work-hardening behavior.
- Reference temperature shifting → use (T - c) rather than T alone to capture symmetry around a calibration/reference point and reduce parameter correlation.
- Smooth yield/flow onset in monotone tests → use softplus/log(1+exp()) or similar smooth transitions in epsilon to mimic an elastic-to-plastic change without discontinuities.
- Ensuring physical sign conventions → models often preserve sigma≈0 at epsilon≈0 for a fixed T unless a thermal misfit term is present; include additive offsets only when residual/thermal stresses are expected.

## Ground Truth Analysis

GT = `2.097*epsilon**3 + 71.356*epsilon**0.2*exp(-0.6018/T) + 3.305*epsilon**3*(T - 370.17)`

Let me expand this:
GT = `2.097*epsilon**3 + 71.356*epsilon**0.2*exp(-0.6018/T) + 3.305*T*epsilon**3 - 1223.3*epsilon**3`

Simplifying:
GT = `(2.097 - 1223.3)*epsilon**3 + 3.305*T*epsilon**3 + 71.356*epsilon**0.2*exp(-0.6018/T)`
GT = `-1221.2*epsilon**3 + 3.305*T*epsilon**3 + 71.356*epsilon**0.2*exp(-0.6018/T)`

So the GT has three basis function components:
1. `T*epsilon**3` (with coefficient ~3.305)
2. `epsilon**3` (with coefficient ~-1221.2)
3. `epsilon**0.2 * exp(-0.6018/T)` (with coefficient ~71.356)

Note: `epsilon**0.2 = epsilon**(1/5)` and `c4/c5 = 5.003/8.314 ≈ 0.6018`

The key term is `epsilon**(1/5) * exp(-c/T)` — this involves both `epsilon**(1/5)` AND `exp(-c/T)` multiplied together.

Now let me check each candidate. The critical question for each is whether it can produce the term `epsilon**0.2 * exp(-const/T)`.

Let me note that `exp(-0.6018/T)` is NOT the same as `exp(a*T)` for any constant `a`. These are fundamentally different functions of T. Similarly, `log(...)` terms, `cos(...)` terms, polynomial terms in T, etc., cannot replicate `exp(-c/T)`.

Let me systematically categorize the candidates:

**Candidates with `exp(T*c)` terms (NOT `exp(c/T)`):**
Candidates 1-11, 16-21, 26, 30, 33, 34, 37, 43-45, 47, 50 — these have `exp(T*c)` which is `exp(c*T)`, not `exp(-c/T)`. These are fundamentally different functions and cannot match.

Wait, but I need to be more careful. Some candidates might have `exp(c/T)` terms.

Let me re-examine candidates with `exp(c/T)`:
- Candidates 22, 24, 28, 29, 32, 36, 39, 40, 41, 42 have `exp(c6/T)` type terms.

For these, `exp(c/T)*epsilon` would need to match `epsilon**(1/5)*exp(-0.6018/T)`. But `epsilon` ≠ `epsilon**(1/5)` — different powers of epsilon cannot be reconciled.

**Candidates with `|epsilon|**(T*c + c)` terms:**
Candidates 4, 12, 14, 15, 31, 45 — these have variable exponents depending on T. This is `epsilon^(aT+b)` which is `epsilon^b * epsilon^(aT)` = `epsilon^b * exp(aT*ln(epsilon))`. This is not equivalent to `exp(-c/T)` times a fixed power of epsilon.

**Candidates with `log(T*c+1)` terms:**
Candidates 48, 49 — `log(T*c+1)` is not `exp(-c/T)`.

**Candidates with `cos(T*c)` or `cos(...)` terms:**
Candidates 23, 27, 35, 46 — trigonometric functions cannot match exponentials.

None of the candidates can produce the essential term `epsilon**(1/5) * exp(-const/T)`.

After careful analysis, **no candidate matches** the GT because none can reproduce the `epsilon**0.2 * exp(-c/T)` term. The candidates either have `exp(c*T)` (wrong T-dependence), `exp(c/T)*epsilon^1` (wrong epsilon power), polynomial/log/cos T-dependence, or variable exponents.
